<tr style="border: 1px #F0F0F0 solid; padding:0px; vertical-align: top; background-color: white"><td style="vertical-align: top; text-align : left; background-color: white; border: 1px #F0F0F0 solid; padding:0px 4px 0px 4px; white-space: nowrap; background-image: url(tbl_bck1100.png)" id="item.EmCare.B22.DE01-help" class="hierarchy"><img src="tbl_spacer.png" alt="." style="background-color: inherit" class="hierarchy"/><img src="tbl_vline.png" alt="." style="background-color: inherit" class="hierarchy"/><img src="tbl_vline.png" alt="." style="background-color: inherit" class="hierarchy"/><img src="tbl_vjoin_end.png" alt="." style="background-color: inherit" class="hierarchy"/><img src="icon-q-display.png" alt="." style="background-color: white; background-color: inherit" title="Display" class="hierarchy"/> EmCare.B22.DE01-help</td><td style="vertical-align: top; text-align : left; background-color: white; border: 1px #F0F0F0 solid; padding:0px 4px 0px 4px" class="hierarchy">&lt;b&gt;Count the number of breaths the child takes per minute&lt;/b&gt; to determine if fast breathing is present.&lt;br /&gt;
It is &lt;b&gt;very important that the child is calm&lt;/b&gt; and still. If the child is moving or crying, you will not be able to get an accurate count of breaths. &lt;br /&gt;
&lt;b&gt;To count the breaths per minute,&lt;/b&gt; use a watch with a second hand or a digital watch. Look for the breathing movement anywhere on the child’s chest or abdomen. &lt;br /&gt;
The number of breaths for &lt;b&gt;‘fast breathing’ depends on the child’s age.&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

	&lt;ul&gt;
		&lt;li&gt;Under 2 months: More than 60 breaths per minute*&lt;/li&gt;
		&lt;li&gt;2 to 11 months: More than 50 breaths per minute&lt;/li&gt;
		&lt;li&gt;12 to 59 months: More than 40 breaths per minute&lt;/li&gt;
	&lt;/ul&gt;

	&lt;p&gt;*In young infants, a second measurement should be taken to confirm, unless there is already another sign of possible serious bacterial infection</td><td style="vertical-align: top; text-align : left; background-color: white; border: 1px #F0F0F0 solid; padding:0px 4px 0px 4px" class="hierarchy">0..1</td><td style="vertical-align: top; text-align : left; background-color: white; border: 1px #F0F0F0 solid; padding:0px 4px 0px 4px" class="hierarchy"><a href="http://hl7.org/fhir/R4/codesystem-item-type.html#item-type-display">display</a></td><td style="vertical-align: top; text-align : left; background-color: white; border: 1px #F0F0F0 solid; padding:0px 4px 0px 4px" class="hierarchy"/><td style="vertical-align: top; text-align : left; background-color: white; border: 1px #F0F0F0 solid; padding:0px 4px 0px 4px" class="hierarchy"/></tr>

<tr style="border: 1px #F0F0F0 solid; padding:0px; vertical-align: top; background-color: white"><td style="vertical-align: top; text-align : left; background-color: white; border: 1px #F0F0F0 solid; padding:0px 4px 0px 4px; white-space: nowrap; background-image: url(tbl_bck11100.png)" id="item.EmCare.B22.DE04-help" class="hierarchy"><img src="tbl_spacer.png" alt="." style="background-color: inherit" class="hierarchy"/><img src="tbl_vline.png" alt="." style="background-color: inherit" class="hierarchy"/><img src="tbl_vline.png" alt="." style="background-color: inherit" class="hierarchy"/><img src="tbl_vline.png" alt="." style="background-color: inherit" class="hierarchy"/><img src="tbl_vjoin_end.png" alt="." style="background-color: inherit" class="hierarchy"/><img src="icon-q-display.png" alt="." style="background-color: white; background-color: inherit" title="Display" class="hierarchy"/> EmCare.B22.DE04-help</td><td style="vertical-align: top; text-align : left; background-color: white; border: 1px #F0F0F0 solid; padding:0px 4px 0px 4px" class="hierarchy">&lt;b&gt;Count the number of breaths the child takes per minute&lt;/b&gt; to determine if fast breathing is present.&lt;br /&gt;
It is &lt;b&gt;very important that the child is calm&lt;/b&gt; and still. If the child is moving or crying, you will not be able to get an accurate count of breaths. &lt;br /&gt;
&lt;b&gt;To count the breaths per minute,&lt;/b&gt; use a watch with a second hand or a digital watch. Look for the breathing movement anywhere on the child’s chest or abdomen. &lt;br /&gt;
The number of breaths for &lt;b&gt;‘fast breathing’ depends on the child’s age.&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

	&lt;ul&gt;
		&lt;li&gt;Under 2 months: More than 60 breaths per minute*&lt;/li&gt;
		&lt;li&gt;2 to 11 months: More than 50 breaths per minute&lt;/li&gt;
		&lt;li&gt;12 to 59 months: More than 40 breaths per minute&lt;/li&gt;
	&lt;/ul&gt;

	&lt;p&gt;*In young infants, a second measurement should be taken to confirm, unless there is already another sign of possible serious bacterial infection</td><td style="vertical-align: top; text-align : left; background-color: white; border: 1px #F0F0F0 solid; padding:0px 4px 0px 4px" class="hierarchy">0..1</td><td style="vertical-align: top; text-align : left; background-color: white; border: 1px #F0F0F0 solid; padding:0px 4px 0px 4px" class="hierarchy"><a href="http://hl7.org/fhir/R4/codesystem-item-type.html#item-type-display">display</a></td><td style="vertical-align: top; text-align : left; background-color: white; border: 1px #F0F0F0 solid; padding:0px 4px 0px 4px" class="hierarchy"/><td style="vertical-align: top; text-align : left; background-color: white; border: 1px #F0F0F0 solid; padding:0px 4px 0px 4px" class="hierarchy"/></tr>

<tr style="border: 1px #F0F0F0 solid; padding:0px; vertical-align: top; background-color: #F7F7F7"><td style="vertical-align: top; text-align : left; background-color: #F7F7F7; border: 1px #F0F0F0 solid; padding:0px 4px 0px 4px; white-space: nowrap; background-image: url(tbl_bck100.png)" id="item.EmCare.B10S2.DE03-help" class="hierarchy"><img src="tbl_spacer.png" alt="." style="background-color: inherit" class="hierarchy"/><img src="tbl_vline.png" alt="." style="background-color: inherit" class="hierarchy"/><img src="tbl_vjoin_end.png" alt="." style="background-color: inherit" class="hierarchy"/><img src="icon-q-display.png" alt="." style="background-color: #F7F7F7; background-color: inherit" title="Display" class="hierarchy"/> EmCare.B10S2.DE03-help</td><td style="vertical-align: top; text-align : left; background-color: #F7F7F7; border: 1px #F0F0F0 solid; padding:0px 4px 0px 4px" class="hierarchy">&lt;b&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;caps&quot;&gt;NORMAL&lt;/span&gt;:&lt;/b&gt; When child breaths &lt;b&gt;IN,&lt;/b&gt; chest wall moves &lt;b&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;caps&quot;&gt;OUT&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;br /&gt;
&lt;b&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;caps&quot;&gt;CHEST&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class=&quot;caps&quot;&gt;INDRAWING&lt;/span&gt;:&lt;/b&gt; When child breaths &lt;b&gt;IN,&lt;/b&gt; chest wall moves &lt;b&gt;IN&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

	&lt;p&gt;Chest indrawing occurs when the child needs to make a greater effort than normal to breathe in. &lt;b&gt;You will look for chest indrawing when the child breathes IN.&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

	&lt;p&gt;In normal breathing, the whole chest wall (upper and lower) and the abdomen move &lt;span class=&quot;caps&quot;&gt;OUT&lt;/span&gt; when the child breathes IN. &lt;b&gt;The child has chest indrawing if the lower chest wall (lower ribs) goes IN when the child breathes IN.&lt;/b&gt;</td><td style="vertical-align: top; text-align : left; background-color: #F7F7F7; border: 1px #F0F0F0 solid; padding:0px 4px 0px 4px" class="hierarchy">0..1</td><td style="vertical-align: top; text-align : left; background-color: #F7F7F7; border: 1px #F0F0F0 solid; padding:0px 4px 0px 4px" class="hierarchy"><a href="http://hl7.org/fhir/R4/codesystem-item-type.html#item-type-display">display</a></td><td style="vertical-align: top; text-align : left; background-color: #F7F7F7; border: 1px #F0F0F0 solid; padding:0px 4px 0px 4px" class="hierarchy"/><td style="vertical-align: top; text-align : left; background-color: #F7F7F7; border: 1px #F0F0F0 solid; padding:0px 4px 0px 4px" class="hierarchy"/></tr>

Put your ear near the child’s mouth because stridor can be difficult to hear. Sometimes you will hear a wet noise if the child’s nose is blocked. Clear the nose, and listen again.&lt;/p&gt;

	&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Be sure to look and listen for stridor when the child is calm.&lt;/b&gt;&lt;br /&gt;
A child who is not very ill may have stridor only when he is crying or upset. However, a child who is calm and also has stridor has a dangerous situation.</td><td style="vertical-align: top; text-align : left; background-color: #F7F7F7; border: 1px #F0F0F0 solid; padding:0px 4px 0px 4px" class="hierarchy">0..1</td><td style="vertical-align: top; text-align : left; background-color: #F7F7F7; border: 1px #F0F0F0 solid; padding:0px 4px 0px 4px" class="hierarchy"><a href="http://hl7.org/fhir/R4/codesystem-item-type.html#item-type-display">display</a></td><td style="vertical-align: top; text-align : left; background-color: #F7F7F7; border: 1px #F0F0F0 solid; padding:0px 4px 0px 4px" class="hierarchy"/><td style="vertical-align: top; text-align : left; background-color: #F7F7F7; border: 1px #F0F0F0 solid; padding:0px 4px 0px 4px" class="hierarchy"/></tr>

<tr style="border: 1px #F0F0F0 solid; padding:0px; vertical-align: top; background-color: #F7F7F7"><td style="vertical-align: top; text-align : left; background-color: #F7F7F7; border: 1px #F0F0F0 solid; padding:0px 4px 0px 4px; white-space: nowrap; background-image: url(tbl_bck100.png)" id="item.EmCare.B11S2.DE02-help" class="hierarchy"><img src="tbl_spacer.png" alt="." style="background-color: inherit" class="hierarchy"/><img src="tbl_vline.png" alt="." style="background-color: inherit" class="hierarchy"/><img src="tbl_vjoin_end.png" alt="." style="background-color: inherit" class="hierarchy"/><img src="icon-q-display.png" alt="." style="background-color: #F7F7F7; background-color: inherit" title="Display" class="hierarchy"/> EmCare.B11S2.DE02-help</td><td style="vertical-align: top; text-align : left; background-color: #F7F7F7; border: 1px #F0F0F0 solid; padding:0px 4px 0px 4px" class="hierarchy">To assess dehydration using the skin pinch&lt;br /&gt;
1. &lt;b&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;caps&quot;&gt;ASK&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/b&gt; the mother to place the child on the examining table so that the child is flat on his back with his arms at his sides (not over his head) and his legs straight. Or, ask the mother to hold the child so he is lying flat on her lap.&lt;br /&gt;
2. &lt;b&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;caps&quot;&gt;USE&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class=&quot;caps&quot;&gt;YOUR&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class=&quot;caps&quot;&gt;THUMB&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class=&quot;caps&quot;&gt;AND&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class=&quot;caps&quot;&gt;FIRST&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class=&quot;caps&quot;&gt;FINGER&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/b&gt; to locate the area on the child’s abdomen halfway between the umbilicus and the side of the abdomen. Do not use your fingertips because this will cause pain. The fold of the skin should be in a line up and down the child’s body.&lt;br /&gt;
3. &lt;b&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;caps&quot;&gt;PICK&lt;/span&gt; UP&lt;/b&gt; all the layers of skin and the tissue underneath them.&lt;br /&gt;
4. &lt;b&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;caps&quot;&gt;HOLD&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/b&gt; the pinch for one second. Then release it.&lt;br /&gt;
5.. &lt;b&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;caps&quot;&gt;LOOK&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/b&gt; to see if the skin pinch goes back &lt;b&gt;very slowly&lt;/b&gt; (more than 2 seconds), &lt;b&gt;slowly,&lt;/b&gt; (less than 2 seconds, but not immediately), or &lt;b&gt;immediately.&lt;/b&gt; If the skin stays up for even a brief time after you release it, decide that the skin pinch goes back slowly.</td><td style="vertical-align: top; text-align : left; background-color: #F7F7F7; border: 1px #F0F0F0 solid; padding:0px 4px 0px 4px" class="hierarchy">0..1</td><td style="vertical-align: top; text-align : left; background-color: #F7F7F7; border: 1px #F0F0F0 solid; padding:0px 4px 0px 4px" class="hierarchy"><a href="http://hl7.org/fhir/R4/codesystem-item-type.html#item-type-display">display</a></td><td style="vertical-align: top; text-align : left; background-color: #F7F7F7; border: 1px #F0F0F0 solid; padding:0px 4px 0px 4px" class="hierarchy"/><td style="vertical-align: top; text-align : left; background-color: #F7F7F7; border: 1px #F0F0F0 solid; padding:0px 4px 0px 4px" class="hierarchy"/></tr>

<tr style="border: 1px #F0F0F0 solid; padding:0px; vertical-align: top; background-color: #F7F7F7"><td style="vertical-align: top; text-align : left; background-color: #F7F7F7; border: 1px #F0F0F0 solid; padding:0px 4px 0px 4px; white-space: nowrap; background-image: url(tbl_bck100.png)" id="item.EmCare.B12S2.DE01-help" class="hierarchy"><img src="tbl_spacer.png" alt="." style="background-color: inherit" class="hierarchy"/><img src="tbl_vline.png" alt="." style="background-color: inherit" class="hierarchy"/><img src="tbl_vjoin_end.png" alt="." style="background-color: inherit" class="hierarchy"/><img src="icon-q-display.png" alt="." style="background-color: #F7F7F7; background-color: inherit" title="Display" class="hierarchy"/> EmCare.B12S2.DE01-help</td><td style="vertical-align: top; text-align : left; background-color: #F7F7F7; border: 1px #F0F0F0 solid; padding:0px 4px 0px 4px" class="hierarchy">&lt;b&gt;A stiff neck may be a sign of meningitis, cerebral malaria or another very severe febrile disease. It requires urgent treatment with injectable antibiotics and referral to a hospital.&lt;/b&gt;&lt;br /&gt;
&lt;b&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;caps&quot;&gt;WATCH&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class=&quot;caps&quot;&gt;THE&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class=&quot;caps&quot;&gt;CHILD&lt;/span&gt;:&lt;/b&gt; While you talk with the caregiver during the assessment, look to see if the child moves and bends his or her neck easily when looking around. If the child is moving and bending his or her neck, the child does not have a stiff neck.&lt;br /&gt;
&lt;b&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;caps&quot;&gt;TEST&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class=&quot;caps&quot;&gt;THE&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class=&quot;caps&quot;&gt;CHILD&lt;/span&gt;:&lt;/b&gt; If you did not see any movement, or if you are not sure, draw the child’s attention to his or her umbilicus or toes. For example, you can shine a flashlight on the toes or umbilicus or tickle the toes to encourage the child to look down. Look to see if the child can bend his or her neck when looking down at his or her umbilicus or toe&lt;br /&gt;
&lt;b&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;caps&quot;&gt;FEEL&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class=&quot;caps&quot;&gt;FOR&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class=&quot;caps&quot;&gt;STIFF&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class=&quot;caps&quot;&gt;NECK&lt;/span&gt;:&lt;/b&gt; If you still have not seen the child bend his or her neck himself, ask the caregiver to help you lay the child on his or her back. Lean over the child, gently support the child’s back and shoulders with one hand. With the other hand, hold the child’s head. Then carefully bend the head forward towards the child’s chest. If the neck bends easily, the child does not have stiff neck. If the neck feels stiff and there is resistance to bending, the child has a stiff neck. Often a child with a stiff neck will cry when you try to bend the neck.</td><td style="vertical-align: top; text-align : left; background-color: #F7F7F7; border: 1px #F0F0F0 solid; padding:0px 4px 0px 4px" class="hierarchy">0..1</td><td style="vertical-align: top; text-align : left; background-color: #F7F7F7; border: 1px #F0F0F0 solid; padding:0px 4px 0px 4px" class="hierarchy"><a href="http://hl7.org/fhir/R4/codesystem-item-type.html#item-type-display">display</a></td><td style="vertical-align: top; text-align : left; background-color: #F7F7F7; border: 1px #F0F0F0 solid; padding:0px 4px 0px 4px" class="hierarchy"/><td style="vertical-align: top; text-align : left; background-color: #F7F7F7; border: 1px #F0F0F0 solid; padding:0px 4px 0px 4px" class="hierarchy"/></tr>

<tr style="border: 1px #F0F0F0 solid; padding:0px; vertical-align: top; background-color: white"><td style="vertical-align: top; text-align : left; background-color: white; border: 1px #F0F0F0 solid; padding:0px 4px 0px 4px; white-space: nowrap; background-image: url(tbl_bck100.png)" id="item.EmCare.B14S2.DE02-help" class="hierarchy"><img src="tbl_spacer.png" alt="." style="background-color: inherit" class="hierarchy"/><img src="tbl_vline.png" alt="." style="background-color: inherit" class="hierarchy"/><img src="tbl_vjoin_end.png" alt="." style="background-color: inherit" class="hierarchy"/><img src="icon-q-display.png" alt="." style="background-color: white; background-color: inherit" title="Display" class="hierarchy"/> EmCare.B14S2.DE02-help</td><td style="vertical-align: top; text-align : left; background-color: white; border: 1px #F0F0F0 solid; padding:0px 4px 0px 4px" class="hierarchy">Pus draining from the eye is a sign of conjunctivitis. Conjunctivitis is an infection of the conjunctiva, the inside surface of the eyelid and the white part of the eye.&lt;br /&gt;
&lt;b&gt;If you do not see pus draining from the eye, look for pus on the conjunctiva or on the eyelids.&lt;/b&gt; Often the pus forms a crust when the child is sleeping and seals the eye shut. You can gently open the eye, making sure that your hands are clean.&lt;br /&gt;
Wash your hands after examining the eye of any child with pus draining from the eye.</td><td style="vertical-align: top; text-align : left; background-color: white; border: 1px #F0F0F0 solid; padding:0px 4px 0px 4px" class="hierarchy">0..1</td><td style="vertical-align: top; text-align : left; background-color: white; border: 1px #F0F0F0 solid; padding:0px 4px 0px 4px" class="hierarchy"><a href="http://hl7.org/fhir/R4/codesystem-item-type.html#item-type-display">display</a></td><td style="vertical-align: top; text-align : left; background-color: white; border: 1px #F0F0F0 solid; padding:0px 4px 0px 4px" class="hierarchy"/><td style="vertical-align: top; text-align : left; background-color: white; border: 1px #F0F0F0 solid; padding:0px 4px 0px 4px" class="hierarchy"/></tr>

<tr style="border: 1px #F0F0F0 solid; padding:0px; vertical-align: top; background-color: white"><td style="vertical-align: top; text-align : left; background-color: white; border: 1px #F0F0F0 solid; padding:0px 4px 0px 4px; white-space: nowrap; background-image: url(tbl_bck100.png)" id="item.EmCare.B14S2.DE03-help" class="hierarchy"><img src="tbl_spacer.png" alt="." style="background-color: inherit" class="hierarchy"/><img src="tbl_vline.png" alt="." style="background-color: inherit" class="hierarchy"/><img src="tbl_vjoin_end.png" alt="." style="background-color: inherit" class="hierarchy"/><img src="icon-q-display.png" alt="." style="background-color: white; background-color: inherit" title="Display" class="hierarchy"/> EmCare.B14S2.DE03-help</td><td style="vertical-align: top; text-align : left; background-color: white; border: 1px #F0F0F0 solid; padding:0px 4px 0px 4px" class="hierarchy">The cornea is usually clear. When clouding of the cornea is present, the cornea &lt;b&gt;may appear clouded or hazy.&lt;/b&gt; The cornea may look the way a glass of water looks when you add a small amount of milk. &lt;b&gt;The clouding may occur in one or both eyes.&lt;/b&gt;&lt;br /&gt;
A child with corneal clouding may keep his or her eyes tightly shut when exposed to light. The light may cause irritation and pain to the child’s eyes. To check the child’s eye, wait for the child to open his or her eye. Or gently pull down the lower eyelid to look for clouding.&lt;br /&gt;
&lt;b&gt;Corneal clouding is a dangerous condition.&lt;/b&gt; It may be the result of vitamin A deficiency that has been made worse by measles. If the corneal clouding is not treated, the cornea can ulcerate and cause blindness. A child with clouding of the cornea needs urgent treatment with vitamin A.</td><td style="vertical-align: top; text-align : left; background-color: white; border: 1px #F0F0F0 solid; padding:0px 4px 0px 4px" class="hierarchy">0..1</td><td style="vertical-align: top; text-align : left; background-color: white; border: 1px #F0F0F0 solid; padding:0px 4px 0px 4px" class="hierarchy"><a href="http://hl7.org/fhir/R4/codesystem-item-type.html#item-type-display">display</a></td><td style="vertical-align: top; text-align : left; background-color: white; border: 1px #F0F0F0 solid; padding:0px 4px 0px 4px" class="hierarchy"/><td style="vertical-align: top; text-align : left; background-color: white; border: 1px #F0F0F0 solid; padding:0px 4px 0px 4px" class="hierarchy"/></tr>

<tr style="border: 1px #F0F0F0 solid; padding:0px; vertical-align: top; background-color: white"><td style="vertical-align: top; text-align : left; background-color: white; border: 1px #F0F0F0 solid; padding:0px 4px 0px 4px; white-space: nowrap; background-image: url(tbl_bck100.png)" id="item.EmCare.B14S2.DE10-help" class="hierarchy"><img src="tbl_spacer.png" alt="." style="background-color: inherit" class="hierarchy"/><img src="tbl_vline.png" alt="." style="background-color: inherit" class="hierarchy"/><img src="tbl_vjoin_end.png" alt="." style="background-color: inherit" class="hierarchy"/><img src="icon-q-display.png" alt="." style="background-color: white; background-color: inherit" title="Display" class="hierarchy"/> EmCare.B14S2.DE10-help</td><td style="vertical-align: top; text-align : left; background-color: white; border: 1px #F0F0F0 solid; padding:0px 4px 0px 4px" class="hierarchy">In measles, &lt;b&gt;a rash begins behind the ears and on the neck. It spreads to the face.&lt;/b&gt; During the next day, the rash spreads to the rest of the body, arms and legs. After 4 to 5 days, the rash starts to fade and the skin may peel.&lt;/p&gt;

	&lt;p&gt;Some children with severe infection may have more rash spread over more of the body. The rash becomes more discoloured (dark brown or blackish), and there is more peeling of the skin. A measles rash does not have vesicles (blisters) or pustules. The rash does not itch.&lt;/p&gt;

	&lt;p&gt;Do not confuse measles with other common childhood rashes such as chicken pox, scabies, or heat rash. Chicken pox rash is a generalized rash with vesicles. Scabies occurs on the hands, feet, ankles, elbows, buttocks and axilla (underarm). It also itches. Heat rash can be a generalized rash with small bumps and vesicles, which itch. A child with heat rash is not sick.</td><td style="vertical-align: top; text-align : left; background-color: white; border: 1px #F0F0F0 solid; padding:0px 4px 0px 4px" class="hierarchy">0..1</td><td style="vertical-align: top; text-align : left; background-color: white; border: 1px #F0F0F0 solid; padding:0px 4px 0px 4px" class="hierarchy"><a href="http://hl7.org/fhir/R4/codesystem-item-type.html#item-type-display">display</a></td><td style="vertical-align: top; text-align : left; background-color: white; border: 1px #F0F0F0 solid; padding:0px 4px 0px 4px" class="hierarchy"/><td style="vertical-align: top; text-align : left; background-color: white; border: 1px #F0F0F0 solid; padding:0px 4px 0px 4px" class="hierarchy"/></tr>

<tr style="border: 1px #F0F0F0 solid; padding:0px; vertical-align: top; background-color: #F7F7F7"><td style="vertical-align: top; text-align : left; background-color: #F7F7F7; border: 1px #F0F0F0 solid; padding:0px 4px 0px 4px; white-space: nowrap; background-image: url(tbl_bck100.png)" id="item.EmCare.B15S2.DE01-help" class="hierarchy"><img src="tbl_spacer.png" alt="." style="background-color: inherit" class="hierarchy"/><img src="tbl_vline.png" alt="." style="background-color: inherit" class="hierarchy"/><img src="tbl_vjoin_end.png" alt="." style="background-color: inherit" class="hierarchy"/><img src="icon-q-display.png" alt="." style="background-color: #F7F7F7; background-color: inherit" title="Display" class="hierarchy"/> EmCare.B15S2.DE01-help</td><td style="vertical-align: top; text-align : left; background-color: #F7F7F7; border: 1px #F0F0F0 solid; padding:0px 4px 0px 4px" class="hierarchy">&lt;span class=&quot;caps&quot;&gt;LOOK&lt;/span&gt; at the skin of the child’s palm. Hold the child’s palm open by grasping it gently from the side. Do not stretch the fingers backwards. This may cause pallor by blocking the blood supply. Compare the colour of the child’s palm with your own palm and with the palms of other children. The child has some palmar pallor if the skin of the child’s palm is pale. The child has severe palmar pallor if the skin of the palm is very pale or so pale that it looks white.</td><td style="vertical-align: top; text-align : left; background-color: #F7F7F7; border: 1px #F0F0F0 solid; padding:0px 4px 0px 4px" class="hierarchy">0..1</td><td style="vertical-align: top; text-align : left; background-color: #F7F7F7; border: 1px #F0F0F0 solid; padding:0px 4px 0px 4px" class="hierarchy"><a href="http://hl7.org/fhir/R4/codesystem-item-type.html#item-type-display">display</a></td><td style="vertical-align: top; text-align : left; background-color: #F7F7F7; border: 1px #F0F0F0 solid; padding:0px 4px 0px 4px" class="hierarchy"/><td style="vertical-align: top; text-align : left; background-color: #F7F7F7; border: 1px #F0F0F0 solid; padding:0px 4px 0px 4px" class="hierarchy"/></tr>

        <text
              value="&lt;b&gt;Count the number of breaths the child takes per minute&lt;/b&gt; to determine if fast breathing is present.&lt;br /&gt;
It is &lt;b&gt;very important that the child is calm&lt;/b&gt; and still. If the child is moving or crying, you will not be able to get an accurate count of breaths. &lt;br /&gt;
&lt;b&gt;To count the breaths per minute,&lt;/b&gt; use a watch with a second hand or a digital watch. Look for the breathing movement anywhere on the child’s chest or abdomen. &lt;br /&gt;
The number of breaths for &lt;b&gt;‘fast breathing’ depends on the child’s age.&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;

	&lt;ul&gt;
		&lt;li&gt;Under 2 months: More than 60 breaths per minute*&lt;/li&gt;
		&lt;li&gt;2 to 11 months: More than 50 breaths per minute&lt;/li&gt;
		&lt;li&gt;12 to 59 months: More than 40 breaths per minute&lt;/li&gt;
	&lt;/ul&gt;

	&lt;p&gt;*In young infants, a second measurement should be taken to confirm, unless there is already another sign of possible serious bacterial infection"/>
        <type value="display"/>
      </item>

1. &lt;b&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;caps&quot;&gt;ASK&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/b&gt; the mother to place the child on the examining table so that the child is flat on his back with his arms at his sides (not over his head) and his legs straight. Or, ask the mother to hold the child so he is lying flat on her lap.&lt;br /&gt;
2. &lt;b&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;caps&quot;&gt;USE&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class=&quot;caps&quot;&gt;YOUR&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class=&quot;caps&quot;&gt;THUMB&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class=&quot;caps&quot;&gt;AND&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class=&quot;caps&quot;&gt;FIRST&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class=&quot;caps&quot;&gt;FINGER&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/b&gt; to locate the area on the child’s abdomen halfway between the umbilicus and the side of the abdomen. Do not use your fingertips because this will cause pain. The fold of the skin should be in a line up and down the child’s body.&lt;br /&gt;
3. &lt;b&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;caps&quot;&gt;PICK&lt;/span&gt; UP&lt;/b&gt; all the layers of skin and the tissue underneath them.&lt;br /&gt;
4. &lt;b&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;caps&quot;&gt;HOLD&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/b&gt; the pinch for one second. Then release it.&lt;br /&gt;
5.. &lt;b&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;caps&quot;&gt;LOOK&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/b&gt; to see if the skin pinch goes back &lt;b&gt;very slowly&lt;/b&gt; (more than 2 seconds), &lt;b&gt;slowly,&lt;/b&gt; (less than 2 seconds, but not immediately), or &lt;b&gt;immediately.&lt;/b&gt; If the skin stays up for even a brief time after you release it, decide that the skin pinch goes back slowly."/>
      <type value="display"/>
    </item>
  </item>

    <type value="boolean"/>
    <required value="true"/>
    <repeats value="false"/>
    <item>
      <extension
                 url="http://hl7.org/fhir/StructureDefinition/questionnaire-itemControl">
        <valueCodeableConcept>

            <system value="http://hl7.org/fhir/questionnaire-item-control"/>

      <linkId value="EmCare.B12S2.DE01-help"/>
      <text
            value="&lt;b&gt;A stiff neck may be a sign of meningitis, cerebral malaria or another very severe febrile disease. It requires urgent treatment with injectable antibiotics and referral to a hospital.&lt;/b&gt;&lt;br /&gt;
&lt;b&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;caps&quot;&gt;WATCH&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class=&quot;caps&quot;&gt;THE&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class=&quot;caps&quot;&gt;CHILD&lt;/span&gt;:&lt;/b&gt; While you talk with the caregiver during the assessment, look to see if the child moves and bends his or her neck easily when looking around. If the child is moving and bending his or her neck, the child does not have a stiff neck.&lt;br /&gt;
&lt;b&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;caps&quot;&gt;TEST&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class=&quot;caps&quot;&gt;THE&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class=&quot;caps&quot;&gt;CHILD&lt;/span&gt;:&lt;/b&gt; If you did not see any movement, or if you are not sure, draw the child’s attention to his or her umbilicus or toes. For example, you can shine a flashlight on the toes or umbilicus or tickle the toes to encourage the child to look down. Look to see if the child can bend his or her neck when looking down at his or her umbilicus or toe&lt;br /&gt;
&lt;b&gt;&lt;span class=&quot;caps&quot;&gt;FEEL&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class=&quot;caps&quot;&gt;FOR&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class=&quot;caps&quot;&gt;STIFF&lt;/span&gt; &lt;span class=&quot;caps&quot;&gt;NECK&lt;/span&gt;:&lt;/b&gt; If you still have not seen the child bend his or her neck himself, ask the caregiver to help you lay the child on his or her back. Lean over the child, gently support the child’s back and shoulders with one hand. With the other hand, hold the child’s head. Then carefully bend the head forward towards the child’s chest. If the neck bends easily, the child does not have stiff neck. If the neck feels stiff and there is resistance to bending, the child has a stiff neck. Often a child with a stiff neck will cry when you try to bend the neck."/>
      <type value="display"/>
    </item>

      <text
            value="The cornea is usually clear. When clouding of the cornea is present, the cornea &lt;b&gt;may appear clouded or hazy.&lt;/b&gt; The cornea may look the way a glass of water looks when you add a small amount of milk. &lt;b&gt;The clouding may occur in one or both eyes.&lt;/b&gt;&lt;br /&gt;
A child with corneal clouding may keep his or her eyes tightly shut when exposed to light. The light may cause irritation and pain to the child’s eyes. To check the child’s eye, wait for the child to open his or her eye. Or gently pull down the lower eyelid to look for clouding.&lt;br /&gt;
&lt;b&gt;Corneal clouding is a dangerous condition.&lt;/b&gt; It may be the result of vitamin A deficiency that has been made worse by measles. If the corneal clouding is not treated, the cornea can ulcerate and cause blindness. A child with clouding of the cornea needs urgent treatment with vitamin A."/>

      <linkId value="EmCare.B14S2.DE10-help"/>
      <text
            value="In measles, &lt;b&gt;a rash begins behind the ears and on the neck. It spreads to the face.&lt;/b&gt; During the next day, the rash spreads to the rest of the body, arms and legs. After 4 to 5 days, the rash starts to fade and the skin may peel.&lt;/p&gt;

	&lt;p&gt;Some children with severe infection may have more rash spread over more of the body. The rash becomes more discoloured (dark brown or blackish), and there is more peeling of the skin. A measles rash does not have vesicles (blisters) or pustules. The rash does not itch.&lt;/p&gt;

	&lt;p&gt;Do not confuse measles with other common childhood rashes such as chicken pox, scabies, or heat rash. Chicken pox rash is a generalized rash with vesicles. Scabies occurs on the hands, feet, ankles, elbows, buttocks and axilla (underarm). It also itches. Heat rash can be a generalized rash with small bumps and vesicles, which itch. A child with heat rash is not sick."/>
      <type value="display"/>
    </item>

Do not stretch the fingers backwards. This may cause pallor by blocking the blood supply. Compare the colour of the child’s palm with your own palm and with the palms of other children. The child has some palmar pallor if the skin of the child’s palm is pale. The child has severe palmar pallor if the skin of the palm is very pale or so pale that it looks white."/>
